//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Airplane_silhouette.svg/20px-Airplane_silhouette.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="400" /></div><div class="pr" style="font-size:91%;width:6em;left:6px"><div><b>OSL</b></div></div></div></div><div style="padding-top:0.2em"><span style="font-size:110%;">Location in <a href="/wiki/Akershus" title="Akershus">Akershus</a> county<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:none;"><div style="font-size:100%;line-height:1.6;font-weight:bold;background:transparent;text-align:left;;">Location of Akershus in Norway</div><div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Norway_Counties_Akershus_Position.svg" class="image"><img alt="Norway Counties Akershus Position.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Norway_Counties_Akershus_Position.svg/220px-Norway_Counties_Akershus_Position.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" /></a></div></div></div></div></span></div></div></div></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black"><a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway"><span style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color:black;">Runways</span></a>\n</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data">\n<table style="width:100%; margin:-2px -1px -1px -1px; border-spacing:0;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="background-color: #e6e6ff">\n<th rowspan="2" style="width: 15%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; border-width:0 1px 0 0; text-align: center;"><a rowspan="2" style="width: 35%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; border-width:0 0 0 1px; text-align: center;">Surface\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background-color: #e6e6ff">\n<th style="width: 20%; border:solid style="text-align: center;">Asphalt/concrete\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n</tbody></table></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black">Statistics (2020)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Passengers</th><td class="infobox-data">9,021,729</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">International</th><td class="infobox-data">3,745,385</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Domestic</th><td class="infobox-data">5,269,549</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Aircraft movements</th><td class="infobox-data">125,428</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Cargo (metric tonnes)</th><td class="infobox-data">181,265</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source:<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Oslo Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a>: <i lang="no">Oslo lufthavn</i>; <a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>OSL</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ENGM</b>), alternatively spelt as <b>Oslo Gardermoen Airport</b> or simply <b>Gardermoen Airport</b>, is the <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> serving <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_towns_and_cities_in_Norway" title="List of towns and cities in Norway">most populous city</a> in the country. A hub for <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wider%C3%B8e" title="Wider\xc3\xb8e">Wider\xc3\xb8e</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a>, it connects to 26 domestic and 158 international destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-directflights_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-directflights-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The airport is located 19 <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical miles</a> (35&#160;km; 22&#160;mi) northeast of Oslo, at <a href="/wiki/Gardermoen,_Norway" title="Gardermoen, Norway">Gardermoen</a> at the border of municipalities <a href="/wiki/Nannestad" title="Nannestad">Nannestad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ullensaker" title="Ullensaker">Ullensaker</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Viken_(county)" title="Viken (county)">Viken</a> county.<sup id="cite_ref-aip_engm_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip_engm-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It has two parallel roughly north\xe2\x80\x93south <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a> measuring 3,600 metres (11,811&#160;ft) and 2,950 metres (9,678&#160;ft) and 71 aircraft stands, of which 50 have <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jet bridges</a>. The airport is connected to the city center by the high-speed railway <a href="/wiki/Gardermoen_Line" title="Gardermoen Line">Gardermoen Line</a> served by <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_State_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian State Railways">mainline trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flytoget" title="Flytoget">Flytoget</a>. The percentage of passengers using public transport to get to and from the airport is one of the highest in the world at nearly 70%.<sup id="cite_ref-Avinor_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avinor-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The ground facilities are owned by Oslo Lufthavn AS, a subsidiary of the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Avinor" title="Avinor">Avinor</a>. Also at the premises is <a href="/wiki/Gardermoen_Air_Station" title="Gardermoen Air Station">Gardermoen Air Station</a>, operated by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Norwegian_Air_Force" title="Royal Norwegian Air Force">Royal Norwegian Air Force</a>. An expansion with a new terminal building and a third pier opened in late April 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The airport location was first used by the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Army" title="Norwegian Army">Norwegian Army</a> from 1940, with the first military airport facilities being built during the 1940s. The airport remained a secondary reserve and airport for chartered flights to <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport,_Fornebu" title="Oslo Airport, Fornebu">Oslo Airport, Fornebu</a>, until 8 October 1998, when the latter was closed and an all-new Oslo Airport opened at Gardermoen, costing 11.4 billion <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_krone" title="Norwegian krone">Norwegian kroner</a> (NOK). \n</p><p>Oslo is additionally served by the much smaller <a href="/wiki/Sandefjord_Airport,_Torp" title="Sandefjord Airport, Torp">Sandefjord Airport, Torp</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Sandefjord" title="Sandefjord">Sandefjord</a>, which situated 119&#160;km to the south of downtown Oslo and primarily used by leisure and <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carriers</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toctext">Airlines and destinations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Passenger"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Plans</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#The_name"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">The tocsection-21"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_and_secondary">Military and secondary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Military and secondary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldiers_at_Gardermoen,_1904.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Soldiers_at_Gardermoen%2C_1904.jpg/220px-Soldiers_at_Gardermoen%2C_1904.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Soldiers_at_Gardermoen%2C_1904.jpg/330px-Soldiers_at_Gardermoen%2C_1904.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Soldiers_at_Gardermoen%2C_1904.jpg/440px-Soldiers_at_Gardermoen%2C_1904.jpg 2x" data-file-width="629" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldiers_at_Gardermoen,_1904.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gardermoen in 1904, while it was still an army camp</div></div></div>\n<p>The Norwegian army started using Gardermoen as a camp in 1740, although it was called Fredericksfeldt until 1788. It was first used by the <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a>, then by the <a href="/wiki/Dragoon" title="Dragoon">dragoons</a>  and in 1789 by the riding marines. The base was also taken into use by the infantry from 1834 and by the artillery from 1860. Tents were solely used until 1860, when the first barracks and stalls were taken into use. Insulated buildings were built around 1900, allowing the camp to be used year-round. By 1925, the base had eleven camps and groups of buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal100_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal100-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The first flight at Gardermoen happened in 1912, and Gardermoen became a station for military flights.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Norway_by_Nazi_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of Norway by Nazi Germany">occupation of Norway by Nazi Germany</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a></i> took over Gardermoen, and built the first proper airport facilities with hangars and two crossing runways, both 2,000 metres (6,600&#160;ft) long. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the airport was taken over by the Norwegian Air Force and made the main air station. Three fighter and one transport squadron were stationed at the Gardermoen.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal100_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal100-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1946, <a href="/wiki/Braathens" title="Braathens">Braathens SAFE</a> established their technical base at the airport, but left two years later. Gardermoen also became the reserve airport for Oslo Airport, Fornebu, when the latter was closed due to fog. From 1946 to 1952, when a longer runway was built at Fornebu, all intercontinental traffic was moved to Gardermoen. Gardermoen grew up as a training field for the commercial airlines and as local airport for <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a>. Some commercial traffic returned again in 1960, when SAS received its first <a href="/wiki/Sud_Aviation_Caravelle" title="Sud Aviation Caravelle">Sud Aviation Caravelle</a> jet aircraft, that could not use the runway at Fornebu until it was extended again in 1962. SAS introduced a direct flight to New York in 1962, but it was quickly terminated.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1972, capacity restraints forced the authorities to move all charter traffic from Fornebu to Gardermoen. However, SAS and Braathens SAFE were allowed to keep their charter services from Fornebu, so they would not have to operate from two bases.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> A former hangar was converted to a terminal building and in 1974 passenger numbers were at 269,000 per year. In 1978, SAS started a weekly flight to New York. In 1983, further restrictions were enforced, and also SAS and Braathens SAFE had to move their charter operations to Gardermoen, increasing passenger numbers that year to 750,000. Several expansions of runway were made after the war, and by the 1985-extension the north-south runway was 3,050 metres (10,010&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Localization_debate">Localization debate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Localization debate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport_location_controversy" title="Oslo Airport location controversy">Oslo Airport location controversy</a></div>\n<p>The first airports to serve Oslo was <a href="/wiki/Kjeller_Airport" title="Kjeller Airport">Kjeller Airport</a> that opened in 1912 and <a href="/wiki/Gressholmen_Airport" title="Gressholmen Airport">Gressholmen Airport</a> that served seaplanes after its opening in 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Norway\'s first airline, <a href="/wiki/Det_Norske_Luftfartrederi" class="mw-redirect" title="Det Norske Luftfartrederi">Det Norske Luftfartrederi</a>, was founded in 1918 and the first scheduled fights were operated by <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Luft_Hansa" title="Deutsche Luft Hansa">Deutsche Luft Hansa</a> to Germany with the opening of Gressholmen.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 1939, a new combined sea and land airport opened at <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport,_Fornebu" title="Oslo Airport, Fornebu">Fornebu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It was gradually expanded, with a runway capable of jet aircraft opening in 1962 and a new terminal building in 1964. But due to its location on a peninsula about 8 kilometres (5.0&#160;mi) from the city center and close to large residential areas, it would not be possible to expand the airport sufficiently to meet all foreseeable demand in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Following the 1972 decision to move charter traffic to Gardermoen, politicians were forced to choose between a "divided solution" that planners stated would eventually force all international traffic to move to Gardermoen, or to build a new airport.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OSLpass.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/OSLpass.JPG/220px-OSLpass.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/OSLpass.JPG/330px-OSLpass.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/OSLpass.JPG/440px-OSLpass.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OSLpass.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Passport control</div></div></div>\n<p>Gardermoen had been proposed as a main airport for Oslo and Eastern Norway as early as 1946, both by the local newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Romerikes_Blad" title="Romerikes Blad">Romerikes Blad</a></i> and by <a href="/wiki/Ludvig_G._Braathen" title="Ludvig G. Braathen">Ludvig G. Braathen</a>, who had just founded Braathens SAFE.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1970, a government report recommended that a new main airport be built at <a href="/wiki/Hob%C3%B8l" title="Hob\xc3\xb8l">Hob\xc3\xb8l</a>, but stated that the time was still not right. The areas were therefore reserved.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> During the 1970s, it became a political priority by the socialist and center parties to reduce state investments in Eastern Norway to stimulate growth in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In 1983, parliament voted to keep the divided solution permanently, and expand Fornebu with a larger terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1985, traffic had increased so much that it became clear that by 1988 all international traffic would have to move to Gardermoen. The areas at Hob\xc3\xb8l had been freed up, and a government report was launched recommending that a new airport be built at Gardermoen, although an airport at <a href="/wiki/Hurum" title="Hurum">Hurum</a> had also been surveyed. However, the report did not look into the need of the Air Force that was stationed at Gardermoen, and was therefore rejected by the parliament the following year. In 1988, a majority of the government chose Hurum as their preferred location, and Minister of Transport <a href="/wiki/Kjell_Borgen" title="Kjell Borgen">Kjell Borgen</a> withdrew from his position. In 1989, new weather surveys from Hurum showed unfavorable conditions. There were large protests from meteorologists and pilots who stated that the surveys were manipulated. Two government committees were appointed, and both concluded that there were no irregularities in the surveys.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since Hurum could no longer be used, the government again recommended Gardermoen as the location. The <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(Norway)" title="Conservative Party (Norway)">Conservative Party</a> instead wanted to build at Hob\xc3\xb8l, but chose to support the Labour Party government\'s proposal to get a new airport as quickly as possible. Parliament passed legislation to build the new main airport at Gardermoen on 8 August 1992. At the same time, it was decided that a high-speed railway was to be built to Gardermoen, so the airport would have a 50% public transport market share.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oslo_airport_Check_in_area.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Oslo_airport_Check_in_area.jpg/220px-Oslo_airport_Check_in_area.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Oslo_airport_Check_in_area.jpg/330px-Oslo_airport_Check_in_area.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Oslo_airport_Check_in_area.jpg/440px-Oslo_airport_Check_in_area.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4709" data-file-height="3362" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oslo_airport_Check_in_area.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Check-in area</div></div></div>\n<p>The choice of Gardermoen has spurred controversy, also after the matter was settled in parliament. In 1994, Engineer <a href="/wiki/Jan_Fredrik_Wiborg" title="Jan Fredrik Wiborg">Jan Fredrik Wiborg</a>, who claimed that falsified weather reports had been made, died after falling from a hotel window in Copenhagen. Circumstances about his death were never fully cleared up and documents about the weather case disappeared.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Standing_Committee_on_Scrutiny_and_Constitutional_Affairs" title="Standing Committee on Scrutiny and Constitutional Affairs">Standing Committee on Scrutiny and Constitutional Affairs</a> held a hearing about the planning process trying to identify any irregularities. An official report was released in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-whistle_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whistle-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>To minimize the effect of using state grants to invest in Eastern Norway, parliament decided that the construction and operation of the airport was to be done by an independent limited company that would be wholly owned by the Civil Airport Administration (today Avinor). This model was chosen to avoid having to deal with public trade unions and to ensure that the construction was not subject to annual grants.<sup id="cite_ref-Bredal,_1998:_39_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bredal,_1998:_39-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> This company was founded in 1992 as Oslo Hovedflyplass AS, but changed its name in 1996 to Oslo Lufthavn. From 1 January 1997, it also took over the operation of Oslo Airport, Fornebu. The company was established with NOK&#160;200 million in share capital. The remaining assets were NOK&#160;2 billion from the sale of Fornebu and NOK&#160;900 million in responsible debt. The remaining funding would come from debt from the state. Total investments for the airport, railways and roads were NOK&#160;22 billion, of which Oslo Lufthavn would have a debt of NOK&#160;11 billion after completion.<sup id="cite_ref-Bredal,_1998:_39_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bredal,_1998:_39-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aircraft_parked_at_the_north_pier_at_Oslo_Airport..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Aircraft_parked_at_the_north_pier_at_Oslo_Airport..jpg/220px-Aircraft_parked_at_the_north_pier_at_Oslo_Airport..jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Aircraft_parked_at_the_north_pier_at_Oslo_Airport..jpg/330px-Aircraft_parked_at_the_north_pier_at_Oslo_Airport..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Aircraft_parked_at_the_north_pier_at_Oslo_Airport..jpg/440px-Aircraft_parked_at_the_north_pier_at_Oslo_Airport..jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aircraft_parked_at_the_north_pier_at_Oslo_Airport..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aircraft parked at the North Pier</div></div></div>\n<p>At Gardermoen there was both an air station and about 270 house owners that had their real estate <a href="/wiki/Eminent_domain" title="Eminent domain">expropriated</a> following parliament\'s decision. NOK&#160;1.7 billion were used to purchase land, including the Air Force. It was the state that expropriated and bought all the land and remained land owner, while Oslo Lufthavn leases the ground from the state.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The first two years were used to demolish and rebuild the air station. This reduced the building area from 120,000 to 41,000 square metres (1,290,000 to 440,000&#160;sq&#160;ft), but gave a more functional design.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal104_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal104-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Construction of the new main airport started on 13 August 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The western runway was already in place, and had been renovated by the Air Force in 1989. A new, eastern runway needed to be built. A hill at the airport was blown away, and the masses used to fill in where needed. The construction of the airport and railway required 13,000 man-years. 220 subcontractors were used, and working accidents were at a third of the national average, without any fatalities.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The last flights to Fornebu took place on 7 October 1998. That night, 300 people and 500 truckloads transported equipment from Fornebu to Gardermoen. Gardermoen opened on 8 October 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal42_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal42-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airlines needed to build their own facilities at Gardermoen. SAS built a complex with 55,000 square metres (590,000&#160;sq&#160;ft), including a technical base, cabin storage, garages and cargo terminals, for NOK&#160;1.398 billion. This included a technical base for their fleet of <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-9" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-9">Douglas DC-9</a> and <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-80" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-80">McDonnell Douglas MD-80</a>-aircraft for NOK&#160;750 million. The cargo handling facility is 21,000 square metres (230,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) and was built in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/Posten_Norge" title="Posten Norge">Posten Norge</a>. SAS also built two lounges in the passenger terminal. Since Braathens had its technical base at <a href="/wiki/Stavanger_Airport,_Sola" title="Stavanger Airport, Sola">Stavanger Airport, Sola</a>, it used NOK&#160;200 million to build facilities. This included a 9,000 square metres (97,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) hangar for six aircraft for NOK&#160;100 million.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flyby_of_Gardermoen_Airport_OSL.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flyby_of_Gardermoen_Airport_OSL.JPG/220px-Flyby_of_Gardermoen_Airport_OSL.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flyby_of_Gardermoen_Airport_OSL.JPG/330px-Flyby_of_Gardermoen_Airport_OSL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Flyby_of_Gardermoen_Airport_OSL.JPG/440px-Flyby_of_Gardermoen_Airport_OSL.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flyby_of_Gardermoen_Airport_OSL.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oslo Airport seen on flyby</div></div></div>\n<p>Parliament decided to build a <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed</a> <a href="/wiki/Airport_rail_link" title="Airport rail link">airport rail link</a> from Oslo to Gardermoen. The 64-kilometre (40&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Gardermoen_Line" title="Gardermoen Line">Gardermoen Line</a> connects <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Central_Station" title="Oslo Central Station">Oslo Central Station</a> (Oslo&#160;)to Gardermoen and onwards to <a href="/wiki/Eidsvoll_Station" title="Eidsvoll Station">Eidsvoll</a>. This line was constructed for 210 kilometres per hour (130&#160;mph) and allows the <a href="/wiki/Flytoget" title="Flytoget">Flytoget</a> train to operate from Oslo&#160;Central station to Gardermoen in nineteen minutes. Just like the airport, the railway was to be financed by the users. The <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_State_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian State Railways">Norwegian State Railways</a> (NSB) established a subsidiary, <i lang="no" title="Norwegian-language text"><a href="/wiki/Flytoget" title="Flytoget">NSB Gardermobanen</a></i>, which would build and own the railway line, as well as operate the airport trains. The company would borrow money from the state, and repay with the profits from operation. During construction of the <a href="/wiki/Romerike_Tunnel" title="Romerike Tunnel">Romerike Tunnel</a>, a leak was made that started draining the water from the lakes above.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The time and cost to repair the leaks meant that the whole railway line budget was exceeded, and the tunnel would not be taken into use until 1 August 1999. Since the rest of the railway was finished, two trains (instead of the intended six), operated using more time from the opening of the new airport.\n</p><p>The main road corridor northwards from Oslo to Gardermoen is <a href="/wiki/European_route_E6" title="European route E6">European Route E6</a>. The E6 was upgraded to six lanes north to Hvam, and to four lanes north to Gardermoen. The E6 runs about 6 kilometres (3.7&#160;mi) east of the airport, so 6 kilometres (3.7&#160;mi) of Norwegian National Road 35 was upgraded to four-lane motorway to connect the E6 to the airport. This connection cost NOK&#160;1 billion. After the opening of the airport, National Road 35 was upgraded west of the airport as a two-lane toll road. Also <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_National_Road_120" title="Norwegian National Road 120">Norwegian National Road 120</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_National_Road_174&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Norwegian National Road 174 (page does not exist)">Norwegian National Road 174</a> were upgraded.<sup id="cite_ref-bredalroad_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredalroad-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_and_growth">Opening and growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Opening and growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gardemoen_airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Gardemoen_airport.jpg/220px-Gardemoen_airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Gardemoen_airport.jpg/330px-Gardemoen_airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Gardemoen_airport.jpg/440px-Gardemoen_airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gardemoen_airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">Icelandair</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 757-200">Boeing 757-200</a> taxiing</div></div></div>\n<p>The first new airline to start scheduled flights was <a href="/wiki/Color_Air" title="Color Air">Color Air</a> operating <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-300">Boeing 737-300</a> jets. The <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airline</a> took advantage of the increased capacity that Gardermoen created to start competing with SAS and Braathens on the routes to Bergen, Trondheim and \xc3\x85lesund. This lasted until October 1999, when Color Air filed for bankruptcy. During this time, all three airlines lost large amounts of money, mainly due to low cabin loads. To win the business market, all three wanted to have the most possible departures per day to other cities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Gardermoen has had considerable problems with <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">fog</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freezing_rain" title="Freezing rain">freezing rain</a>, and has several times had a complete close-down. This was also a problem at Fornebu, and reported to be at Hurum as well. On average, there is super cooled rain three times per month during the winter.<sup id="cite_ref-whistle_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whistle-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The use of <a href="/wiki/Deicing" class="mw-redirect" title="Deicing">deicing</a> fluids is restricted since the area underneath the airport contains the Tandrum Delta, one of the country\'s largest uncontained quaternary <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifers</a> (underground water systems).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On 14 December, 1998, a combination of freezing fog and supercooled rain caused glaze at Gardermoen. At least twenty aircraft engines were damaged by ice during take-off, and five aircraft needed to make <a href="/wiki/Emergency_landing" title="Emergency landing">precautionary landings</a> with only one working engine.<sup id="cite_ref-whistle_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whistle-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On 18 January, 2006, an <a href="/wiki/Infratek" title="Infratek">Infratek</a> deicing system was set up, that uses infrared heat in large hangar tents. It was hoped that it could reduce chemical deicers by 90%, but the technique has proved unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1999, <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a> briefly operated a flight between Oslo and <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>/<a href="/wiki/St._Paul,_MN" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Paul, MN">St. Paul, MN</a>, United States, for several months, before the flight was cancelled due to poor load factors.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Northwest had previously served the airport in 1987 with nonstop flights operated with <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-40" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10-40">McDonnell Douglas DC-10-40</a> wide body jetliners several days a week to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">JFK, New York</a> with continuing direct service to <a href="/wiki/Memphis_International_Airport" title="Memphis International Airport">Memphis International Airport</a> (MEM) and <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis%E2%80%93Saint_Paul_International_Airport" title="Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93Saint Paul International Airport">Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93Saint Paul International Airport</a> (MSP).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In October 2001, the only remaining intercontinental flight, to <a href="/wiki/Newark_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Newark Airport">Newark Airport</a> (EWR), with <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a> (SAS) operated <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767-300</a> aircraft, was discontinued, due to a slump in air travel following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_Attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="September 11 Attacks">9/11</a>. In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">Continental Airlines</a> (now <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>) resumed service on this route using <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 757-200">Boeing 757-200</a> respectively. <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> suspended winter service on the route in 2015, then discontinued the service completely in 2017. Scandinavian Airlines also started a direct service from Oslo to <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also in 1999, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_International_Airlines" title="Pakistan International Airlines">Pakistan International Airlines</a> (PIA) became the first Asian airline to touchdown in Oslo, commencing its first flights to the city to and from <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a>. The return flights had a stopover at <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen Airport</a> before continuing onward to Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a> launched flights to Bangkok, New York \xe2\x80\x93 JFK, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale%E2%80%93Hollywood_International_Airport" title="Fort Lauderdale\xe2\x80\x93Hollywood International Airport">Fort Lauderdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oakland_International_Airport" title="Oakland International Airport">Oakland (San Francisco)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orlando_International_Airport" title="Orlando International Airport">Orlando</a> with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a> jetliners and Dubai, Agadir and Marrakech with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800</a> jets,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2018)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways" title="Thai Airways">Thai Airways</a> to <a href="/wiki/Suvarnabhumi_Airport" title="Suvarnabhumi Airport">Bangkok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> to <a href="/wiki/Doha_International_Airport" title="Doha International Airport">Doha</a>, Emirates to <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a>. In 2012, the airport opened a new 650-square-meter (7,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) VIP terminal exclusively used for the royal family, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Norway" title="Prime Minister of Norway">prime minister</a> and foreign heads of state and government.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oslo_Airport_interior_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OslConnect.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/OslConnect.JPG/220px-OslConnect.JPG" href="/wiki/File:14-09-02-oslo-RalfR-469.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/14-09-02-oslo-RalfR-469.jpg/220px-14-09-02-oslo-RalfR-469.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/14-09-02-oslo-RalfR-469.jpg/330px-14-09-02-oslo-RalfR-469.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/14-09-02-oslo-RalfR-469.jpg/440px-14-09-02-oslo-RalfR-469.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:14-09-02-oslo-RalfR-469.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:OSL_tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/OSL_tower.jpg/220px-OSL_tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="310" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/OSL_tower.jpg/330px-OSL_tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/OSL_tower.jpg/440px-OSL_tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3656" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:OSL_tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ATC tower</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport covers an area of 13 square kilometres (5.0&#160;sq&#160;mi) and is modeled partially on <a href="/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" title="Hartsfield\xe2\x80\x93Jackson Atlanta International Airport">Hartsfield\xe2\x80\x93Jackson Atlanta International Airport</a>, with two parallel runways and a single terminal with two piers on a single line.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal42_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal42-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bredal45_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal45-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Oslo Airport is located 19 <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical miles</a> (35&#160;km; 22&#160;mi) north-northeast of Oslo city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-aip_engm_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip_engm-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal">Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The passenger terminal covers 265,000 square metres (2,850,000&#160;sq&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-bredal42_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal42-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The airport has 72 gates, of which 44 are bridge-connected and 28 are remote stands.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal42_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal42-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Domestic gates are located in the west and north pier (gates A, B, C), while gates for international flights are in the east and north pier (gates D, E), with gates for non-Schengen area flights at the end of the east pier (gates F).<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Four gates near the end of the east pier are flexigates where doors can be opened or closed to switch between Schengen and non-Schengen flights.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> EU controllers have been somewhat sceptical of the Schengen/non-Schengen flexigates, and there were a few incidents where the wrong doors were opened so that passengers who should have gone through the <a href="/wiki/Border_control" title="Border control">border control</a> did not.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The new pier that extends northwards from the terminal was opened in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> To compensate for the gates lost in the interim period, an extra pier south of and parallel to the west wing was constructed in 2012 for domestic flights. This "pier south" has eight gates that all lack jet bridges, and was intended for demolition after five years.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The extension gives a capacity of 32 million; in 2016, 25.7 million passengers used the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-oslinfo_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oslinfo-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The airport is "silent", so announcements for flights are only done in the immediate vicinity of the gate. There is a playground in both the domestic and international sections, and a quiet room in the domestic section. Medical personnel are stationed at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because of the airport\'s customs procedures for connecting passengers (the luggage has to be picked up, shown to customs and checked in when connecting from international to domestic flights), some transit passengers are now avoiding Oslo Airport and finding other routing options when possible. The process of clearing customs before connecting from an international to a domestic flight is not unique for Oslo Airport, as it is the same process used at international airports in the United States and some other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>About half the airport operator\'s income is from retail revenue. There are twenty restaurants providing food or drink service, in addition to stores and other services including banks and post. In all, 8,000 square metres (86,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) are used for restaurants, stores and non-aviation services.<sup id="cite_ref-oslinfo_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oslinfo-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oslshop_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oslshop-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The departure <a href="/wiki/Duty-free_shop" title="Duty-free shop">duty-free shop</a> is 1,530 square metres (16,500&#160;sq&#160;ft) and the largest in Europe. The shop is located in front of the international concourse, taking up a large part of the terminal\'s width.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The airport has attempted to funnel all passengers through the duty-free.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Signs that were to hinder passengers from walking outside the duty-free were in 2008 removed after criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Arriving passengers have access to a smaller duty-free shop in the baggage claim area.\n</p><p>In addition to the main terminal, the airport operates its own VIP lounge for the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Royal Family">Norwegian Royal Family</a>, for members of the Norwegian government and members of foreign royal families and governments.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The GA-terminal, located on the west side of the airport, services GA-aircraft, <a href="/wiki/Business_jet" title="Business jet">executive jets</a> and ambulance aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The cargo terminal is located just southwest of the main terminal and has 7 gates for cargo aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal42_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal42-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The airport is heated using <a href="/wiki/District_heating" title="District heating">district heating</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_gradient" title="Geothermal gradient">geothermal</a> source. The airport uses 32.6&#160;GWh/year for heating and 5.6&#160;GWh/year for cooling. In addition, the airport uses 110&#160;GWh/year of electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Art and architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Architects were Aviaplan, a joint venture between the agencies <a href="/wiki/Nordic_%E2%80%94_Office_of_Architecture" title="Nordic \xe2\x80\x94 Office of Architecture">Nordic \xe2\x80\x94 Office of Architecture</a>, Niels Torp, Skaarup &amp; Jespersen and Hjellnes Cowi.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal45_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal45-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The main architect was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gudmund_Stokke&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gudmund Stokke (page does not exist)">Gudmund Stokke</a>. The terminal building has a light, floating roof that results in simple construction. First the walls were erected, and a roof put on top. Afterwards internal facilities were added. The roof is held up by wooden reefers. The main construction materials are wood, metal and glass. The airlines were required to follow the same design rules for their buildings as the terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main art on the landside of the airport is <i>Alexis</i>, consisting of six steel sculptures in stainless steel created by <a href="/wiki/Per_Inge_Bj%C3%B8rlo" title="Per Inge Bj\xc3\xb8rlo">Per Inge Bj\xc3\xb8rlo</a>. On the airside, Carin Wessel used 30,000 metres (98,000&#160;ft) of thread to make the impression of clouds and webs, named <i>Ad Astra</i>. Anna Karin Rynander and Per-Olof Sandberg cooperated in making two installations: <i>The Marathon Dancers</i>, located in the baggage claim area, is a set of two electronic boards that show a dancing person. <i>Sound Refreshment Station</i>, of which six are located in the departure areas, are sound "showers" that make refreshing sounds when a person is immediately under them. Sidsel Westb\xc3\xb8 etched the glass walls. In the check-in area, there are small boxes under the floor with glass ceilings that contain curiosities. As well as the custom-made art, several existing sculptures and paintings were bought.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> At the National Road 35 and European Route E6 junction, <a href="/wiki/Vebj%C3%B8rn_Sand" title="Vebj\xc3\xb8rn Sand">Vebj\xc3\xb8rn Sand</a> built a 14-metre (46&#160;ft) statue named the <i>Kepler Star</i>. It consists of two internally illuminated <a href="/wiki/Kepler%E2%80%93Poinsot_polyhedron" title="Kepler\xe2\x80\x93Poinsot polyhedron">Kepler\xe2\x80\x93Poinsot polyhedrons</a>, appearing like a giant star in the sky after dark.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways_and_air_traffic_control">Runways and air traffic control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Runways and air traffic control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport has two parallel runways, aligned 01/19. The west runway 01L/19R is 3,600 by 45 metres (11,811&#160;ft \xc3\x97&#160;148&#160;ft), while the east runway 01R/19L is 2,950 by 45 metres (9,678&#160;ft \xc3\x97&#160;148&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-aip_engm_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip_engm-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Both have <a href="/wiki/Taxiway" title="Taxiway">taxiways</a>, allowing 80 air movements per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-bredal42_32-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredal42-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The runways are equipped with <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system#Ils_categories" title="Instrument landing system">CAT IIIA instrument landing system</a><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and the airport is supervised by a 91-metre (299&#160;ft) tall <a href="/wiki/Control_tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Control tower">control tower</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oslinfo_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oslinfo-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Once departing aircraft are 15 kilometres (9&#160;mi) away from the airport, responsibility is taken over by <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Air_Traffic_Control_Center" title="Oslo Air Traffic Control Center">Oslo Air Traffic Control Center</a>, which supervises the airspace with <a href="/wiki/Hauk%C3%A5sen_Radar" title="Hauk\xc3\xa5sen Radar">Hauk\xc3\xa5sen Radar</a>. The airport has two ground radars, on the far sides of each of the runways. Both at the gates and along the taxiways, there is an automatic system of lights that guide the aircraft. On the tarmac, these are steered by the radar, while they are controlled by motion sensors at the gate.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are three <a href="/wiki/Deicing" class="mw-redirect" title="Deicing">deicing</a> platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-aip_engm_2-6_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip_engm_2-6-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Fire_station" title="Fire station">fire stations</a> each have three fire cars, and is part of the municipal fire department.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Meteorological services are operated by the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Meteorological_Institute" title="Norwegian Meteorological Institute">Norwegian Meteorological Institute</a>, which has 12 weather stations and 16 employees at the airport. This includes Norway\'s first aeronautic information service and a self-briefing room, in addition to briefings from professionals.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Restrictions on air movements apply overnight from 23:00 to 06:00, although permitted if landing from and taking off to the north.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_station">Air station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Air station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gardermoen_Air_Station" title="Gardermoen Air Station">Gardermoen Air Station</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Norwegian_Air_Force" title="Royal Norwegian Air Force">Royal Norwegian Air Force</a> has an air base at Gardermoen, located at the north side of the passenger terminal at Oslo Airport. The base dates from 1994 and houses the 335-Squadron that operates three <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_C-130_Hercules" title="Lockheed C-130 Hercules">Lockheed C-130 Hercules</a> transport planes. The airbase also handles nearly all military freight going abroad. The Air Force has a compact 41,000 square metres (440,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) building space, with a maximum walking distance of 400 metres (1,300&#160;ft). The station is built so that it can quickly be expanded if necessary, without having to claim areas used by the civilian section. The military also use the civilian terminals for their passenger transport needs, and send 200,000 people with chartered and scheduled flights from the main terminal each year.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\nThe airforce station serves as the main entering point for VIPs and officials going to Norway.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Avinor" title="Avinor">Avinor</a></div>\n<p>The airport is owned by Oslo Lufthavn AS, a limited company wholly owned by <a href="/wiki/Avinor" title="Avinor">Avinor</a>, a state-owned company responsible for operating 46 Norwegian airports. In 2010, Oslo Lufthavn had a revenue of NOK 3,693 million, giving an income of NOK 1,124 million before tax. The profit from the airport is largely paid to Avinor, who uses it to cross-<a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">subsidise</a> operating deficits from smaller primary and regional airport throughout the country. At the end of 2010, Oslo Lufthavn had 439 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-ar2010_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar2010-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company has a subsidiary, Oslo Lufthavn Eiendom AS, which is responsible for developing commercial real estate around the airport. It owns one airport hotel run by the <a href="/wiki/Radisson_Hotels" title="Radisson Hotels">Radisson Blu</a> chain, the office building and conference center Flyporten, which along with the hotel features 60 conference rooms, and the employee parking lot. A second hotel, Park Inn, was opened in September 2010.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Gardermoen has direct connections to just over 160 destinations. In addition, there are up to several charter destinations, depending on the season. The domestic network is dominated by Norwegian and SAS, which mainly fly commercially on the main airport network. In addition, Wider\xc3\xb8e operates tender routes on a contract with the Ministry of Transport and Communications.\n</p><p>The international route network is focused on European destinations. SAS, Norwegian and a number of major European network companies fly with high frequency between Gardermoen and the Nordic capitals, as well as the major cities in Western Europe and Eastern Europe. In addition, it flies directly to a larger number of destinations in the Mediterranean countries, although with somewhat lower frequency and variations in the summer months.\n</p><p>Until 2020, Gardermoen had a relatively large increase in the number of long-distance routes. This growth was largely driven by Norwegian\'s investment in longer routes. When the coronavirus pandemic came to Norway in March 2020, Norwegian had to close down its Long-Haul fleets after a short time, because there was not a sufficient customer base.\n</p><p>However, companies such as Qatar Airways and Emirates also contributed to the long-distance increase. In the spring of 2019, Hainan Airlines opened a direct route between Oslo and Beijing. As of 2019, a number of charter flights were also offered from Gardermoen under the auspices of various travel operators, distributed throughout the year. Among these operators were Ving, Apollo and TUI. During the summer months, destinations around the Mediterranean were best represented until 2020 (especially holiday destinations in Spain, Greece and Turkey), while in the winter, direct flights is offered to intercontinental destinations, including Cuba, Gambia, Canary Islands, Cape Verde, Mexico and Thailand.:<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td> <a id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Oslo Airport has a <a href="/wiki/Catchment_area_(human_geography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catchment area (human geography)">catchment area</a> of 2.5 million people, including most of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Norway" title="Eastern Norway">Eastern Norway</a> and 0.3 million people in Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-stat2010_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat2010-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, Oslo Airport served 27,482,315 passengers, 181,265 tonnes (178,402 long tons; 199,810 short tons) of cargo and 242,555 aircraft movements. Within Europe in 2017, Oslo Airport ranked as the nineteenth-busiest. It is the second-busiest airport in the Nordic countries, after <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen Airport</a>. The busiest route is to Trondheim, with over 2 million passengers. Along with the domestic routes to Bergen and Stavanger, and the international routes to Copenhagen and Stockholm, Oslo Airport served five of the twenty-five busiest routes in the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">EEA</a>, all with more than one million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-norskbane_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norskbane-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_traffic">Annual traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Annual traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1017906329">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output style="visibility:hidden;color:transparent;">0</span>1.0%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport_Station" title="Oslo Airport Station">Oslo Airport Station</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flytoget_at_Gardermoen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Flytoget_at_Gardermoen.jpg/220px-Flytoget_at_Gardermoen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Flytoget_at_Gardermoen.jpg/330px-Flytoget_at_Gardermoen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Flytoget_at_Gardermoen.jpg/440px-Flytoget_at_Gardermoen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flytoget_at_Gardermoen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/GMB_Class_71" title="GMB Class 71">Class 71</a> <a href="/wiki/Flytoget" title="Flytoget">Airport Express Train</a> at <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport_Station" title="Oslo Airport Station">Oslo Airport Station</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Situated about 47 kilometres (29&#160;mi) from the city center,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Oslo Airport offers extensive public transporting services. The airport has one of the world\'s highest levels of <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> usage, with a share of nearly 70%.<sup id="cite_ref-Avinor_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avinor-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 64 kilometres (40&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Gardermoen_Line" title="Gardermoen Line">Gardermoen Line</a> opened the same day as the airport, and runs in a tunnel below the airport facilities, where <a href="/wiki/Gardermoen_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Gardermoen Station">Gardermoen Station</a> is located below the terminal. The <a href="/wiki/Flytoget" title="Flytoget">Flytoget</a> airport express train operates to <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Central_Station" title="Oslo Central Station">Oslo Central Station</a> six times per hour in 19 to 22 minutes, with three services continuing onwards via five intermediate stations to <a href="/wiki/Drammen_Station" title="Drammen Station">Drammen Station</a>. (On Saturdays and Sundays, the frequency is three times per hour.)<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The Airport Express Train has a 34% ground transport share.<sup id="cite_ref-pubtrans_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pubtrans-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vy_(transport_operator)" title="Vy (transport operator)">Vy</a> also operates from the airport, both a <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Commuter_Rail" title="Oslo Commuter Rail">commuter train</a> service to <a href="/wiki/Eidsvoll" title="Eidsvoll">Eidsvoll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kongsberg" title="Kongsberg">Kongsberg</a>, and a regional service north to <a href="/wiki/Innlandet" title="Innlandet">Innlandet</a> and south to <a href="/wiki/Vestfold_og_Telemark" title="Vestfold og Telemark">Vestfold og Telemark</a>. Both offer services to Oslo, and the latter allows direct service to <a href="/wiki/Sandefjord_Airport,_Torp" title="Sandefjord Airport, Torp">Sandefjord Airport, Torp</a>. Five daily express trains operated by <a href="/wiki/SJ_Norge" class="mw-redirect" title="SJ Norge">SJ Norge</a> to <a href="/wiki/Trondheim" title="Trondheim">Trondheim</a> stop at the airport, including one <a href="/wiki/Night_trains_of_Norway" title="Night trains of Norway">night train</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Oslo Airport Express Coach serves the airport, from Oslo, <a href="/wiki/Fredrikstad" title="Fredrikstad">Fredrikstad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ski,_Norway" title="Ski, Norway">Ski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gj%C3%B8vik" title="Gj\xc3\xb8vik">Gj\xc3\xb8vik</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In addition, most express buses from other parts of Norway stop at the airport. The local transport authority, <a href="/wiki/Ruter" title="Ruter">Ruter</a>, operates a number of services to Oslo Airport from nearby places.\n</p><p>The airport is located 2 kilometres (1.2&#160;mi) from <a href="/wiki/European_route_E16" title="European route E16">European Route E16</a>, and 6 kilometres (3.7&#160;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/European_route_E6" title="European route E6">European Route E6</a> and connect to them as a four-lane motorway. The E6 runs south with four lanes to Oslo, and northwards with four lanes towards <a href="/wiki/Oppland" title="Oppland">Oppland</a>, Hedmark and Central Norway. E16 connects with two lanes westward towards Buskerud and eastward towards Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-bredalroad_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bredalroad-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> All these directions are <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">toll roads</a>, at least in part. There are 11,400 parking spaces at the airport,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> as well as taxi stands and rental car facilities.\n</p><p><b>Taxi</b>\n</p><p>There are several companies offering services at Oslo Airport. In order to check companies, rates and book a taxi, the passenger must go to the information desk at the Arrivals Hall of the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The taxi rank is located just outside the arrivals hall.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans">Plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Oslo Airport has experienced rapid increases in passenger numbers during the last decade, already exceeding its original capacity limit of 17 million passengers. As a result, the Norwegian Air Transport Authority, Avinor, approved plans on 19 January, 2011, for an expansion of OSL with Terminal 2 (North Pier). Finished in Spring 2017, the expansion involved construction of a new pier located directly after security checkpoint with eleven new air bridges, six remote stands, a new arrivals- and departure-hall and a new <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling_system" title="Baggage handling system">baggage handling system</a>. A total of 117,000 square meters were added, resulting a total of 265,000 square meters today. OSL can now handle 32 million passengers annually.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Yet, before the North Pier was finished, OSL have invested further plans to expand the international terminal with six new wide-body airliner gates for more direct flights to destinations outside of Europe. The expansion is set to begin in 2017 and will be finished between 2019 and 2021<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\nOnce the intercontinental expansion is finished, the airport will be able to accommodate the double-decker <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> This would also advance point-to-point flying and fix the major issue where Norwegians are traveling to larger hub-and-spoke airports in Europe in order to reach their final destination, because OSL (both the market and airport\'s size) is too small to handle a global flight network.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Another phase will be added later on to bring the total capacity to 35 million passengers annually through the T2-project.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\nIf passenger traffic continues to grow and if the capacity will be surpassed beyond the capabilities, OSL and Avinor will call out for a master phase (as situated in the Master Plan 2012\xe2\x80\x932050), including extension of the North Pier by another 100 meters, adding a third runway with a free-standing pier between it and the existing Eastern runway, as well as a new terminal to the southeast area of the current international terminal (by where Park Inn is located).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Government of Oslo has debated if a third runway in the future will be reliable. If they approve, the runway will not be finished until 2030 at the earliest. Avinor has discovered the existing runway capacity will be saturated by 2030, but critics have pointed out that larger hubs as <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a> in London only operates with two runways. However, such airports tend to suffer of major delays and chaos at their schedules. Oslo had 253,542 movements against 474,087 at Heathrow in 2017. Former <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Transport_and_Communications_(Norway)" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of Transport and Communications (Norway)">Minister of Transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liv_Signe_Navarsete" title="Liv Signe Navarsete">Liv Signe Navarsete</a> (<a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Norway)" title="Centre Party (Norway)">Center</a>), has stated that spreading the traffic between the two airports (RYG is closed on permanent basis) will result in inconvenience for passengers and a massive need for inter-airport ground transportation, but has announced she is opposed to a third runway.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Avinor is facing large costs of extending <a href="/wiki/STOLport" title="STOLport">short runways</a> in rural locations or replacing such airports during the 2020s decade, so a third runway at Oslo is less prioritized. However, as of December 2017, construction of a nearby city directly to the east of OSL has been officially approved, nicknamed "the Gate to Europe", in which a third runway and a third terminal are part of the project.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B8rn_Kjos" title="Bj\xc3\xb8rn Kjos">Bj\xc3\xb8rn Kjos</a> has announced that the airline has ambitions to evolve Gardermoen into a major global hub between North America and South Asia. Kjos stated; "We could have received tons of traffic from all around the world. Oslo could have been one of the largest hubs in Europe, and could have competed against the large ones in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">DXB</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamad_International_Airport" title="Hamad International Airport">DOH</a>). He guarantees the transatlantic routes will be significantly shorter via Northern Europe, which will lead to increased efficiency and satisfaction for the travelers and for the economy. Norwegian is currently disallowed to fly direct over Russian territory by their Air Traffic Authorities, meaning that negotiation is the only solution.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_name">The name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: The name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><i>Gardermoen</i> is a compound of the farm name <i>Garder</i> and the finite form of <i>mo</i> \'moor; drill ground\' (thus \'the moor belonging to the farm Garder\'). The farm is first mentioned in 1328 (<i>Gar\xc3\xb0ar</i>), and the name is the plural of <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Norse</a> <i>gar\xc3\xb0r</i> \'<a href="/wiki/Fence" title="Fence">fence</a>\'. The meaning is probably \'enclosure; fenced fields\'.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Delays_in_2012">Delays in 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Delays in 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>According to <a href="/wiki/EUROCONTROL" class="mw-redirect" title="EUROCONTROL">EUROCONTROL</a>, the "European Organisation for the Safety of Air Navigation", Gardermoen had the most delays per flight of all airports in Europe in July 2012. As a consequence of the delays, which apparently were caused by a lack of air traffic controllers, several airlines are demanding <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_krone" title="Norwegian krone">NOK</a> 100 million in compensation from <a href="/wiki/Avinor" title="Avinor">Avinor</a>. The head of Avinor said that the agency may pay compensation to the airlines, also saying that "they did not get a good enough product last summer".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a Airport</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport,_Fornebu" title="Oslo Airport, Fornebu">Oslo-Fornebu Airport</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gardermoen_Air_Station" title="Gardermoen Air Station">Gardermoen Air Station</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport_Station" title="Oslo Airport Station">Oslo Airport Station (railways)</a></li>\n<li><a
